  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c9f76c78-dd4c-4bbb-8332-353ca13694b1'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer6793894145169553375"><i>A missing God.</i><br/><i>A library with the secrets to the universe. </i><br/><i>A woman too busy to notice her heart slipping away.</i><br/><br/>Carolyn's not so different from the other people around her. She likes guacamole and cigarettes and steak. She knows how to use a phone. Clothes are a bit tricky, but everyone says nice things about her outfit with the Christmas sweater over the gold bicycle shorts.</span>
  <span id="freeText6793894145169553375" style="display:none"><i>A missing God.</i><br /><i>A library with the secrets to the universe. </i><br /><i>A woman too busy to notice her heart slipping away.</i><br /><br />Carolyn's not so different from the other people around her. She likes guacamole and cigarettes and steak. She knows how to use a phone. Clothes are a bit tricky, but everyone says nice things about her outfit with the Christmas sweater over the gold bicycle shorts. After all, she was a normal American herself once.  <br /><br />That was a long time ago, of course. Before her parents died. Before she and the others were taken in by the man they called Father. In the years since then, Carolyn hasn't had a chance to get out much. Instead, she and her adopted siblings have been raised according to Father's ancient customs. They've studied the books in his Library and learned some of the secrets of his power. And sometimes, they've wondered if their cruel tutor might secretly be God.  Now, Father is missing—perhaps even dead—and the Library that holds his secrets stands unguarded. And with it, control over all of creation. <br /><br />As Carolyn gathers the tools she needs for the battle to come, fierce competitors for this prize align against her, all of them with powers that far exceed her own. But Carolyn has accounted for this. And Carolyn has a plan. The only trouble is that in the war to make a new God, she's forgotten to protect the things that make her human. <br /><br />Populated by an unforgettable cast of characters and propelled by a plot that will shock you again and again, <i>The Library at Mount Char</i> is at once horrifying and hilarious, mind-blowingly alien and heartbreakingly human, sweepingly visionary and nail-bitingly thrilling—and signals the arrival of a major new voice in fantasy.<br /><br /><i>From the Hardcover edition.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6793894145169553375" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/630029-what-the-hell-am-i-supposed-to-read-now">What the hell am I supposed to read now? I&#39;m chomping at the bit for something that will blow my mind for at least a week like this did. Any suggestions?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_630029'><a id="like_count_community_question_630029" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/630029?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">70 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F26892110-the-library-at-mount-char">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/630029-what-the-hell-am-i-supposed-to-read-now">4 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/630029-what-the-hell-am-i-supposed-to-read-now">See all 29 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/32322996-scott-hawkins"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1430050224i/32322996._UX100_CR0,25,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/32322996-scott-hawkins">Scott Hawkins</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Hi Kelsey,<br/><br/>I was just typing up a reply saying something like "I love playing the recommend-me-a-book game, but it's tough to come up with good recomme<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Hi Kelsey,<br /><br />I was just typing up a reply saying something like "I love playing the recommend-me-a-book game, but it's tough to come up with good recommendations if I only know one book that you--" <br /><br />Then I remembered I'm on goodreads, and that's not really a problem. It sucks getting old. Anyway, I have recommendations! All of these are things that left me reeling for at least a couple of days. <br /><br />You might try The Virgin Suicides by Jeffrey Eugenides. It's a slow build, but it's got a kind of surreal, not-quite-a-dream, trapped-in-the-suburbs vibe that I really like. I pull that one out and reread it every couple of years. The audiobook version is also excellent.<br /><br />Kind of in that same surreal/literary vein, there's one called The Orphan Master's Son that I absolutely love. In terms of sheer tour-de-force literary technique, it's one of the strongest books I've ever read. It is PITCH BLACK DARK, however. <br /><br />This isn't one I recommend to everyone, but you might try a graphic novel called <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38333.Black_Hole?from_search=true&amp;search_version=service" rel="nofollow noopener">Black Hole</a> by a guy named Charles Burns. It's kind of hard to describe. There's no superheroes or anything--it's about this sort of v.d. epidemic in the 1970s suburbs that turns teenagers into kinda-sorta monsters? Again, dreamy and surreal. <br /><br />I highly, highly recommend Stephen King's The Long Walk. It's one of his first--he wrote it when he was (I think) an undergrad, well before Carrie. It's a little raw in terms of technique, but it's a sledgehammer of a book. <br /><br />Wizard of Earthsea by Ursula Le Guin is one of my all-time favorites. <br /><br />Last but not least--this one's kind of a long shot in that I didn't see a lot of hard sci-fi in your list, but if you're in the mood to branch out you might try one called Pushing Ice by Alastair Reynolds. It's a real page-turner, and also mind-blowing in a hard science fiction kind of way. <br /><br />Hopefully at least one of those works for you. <br /><br />Scott<br /><a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_2448740397" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2448740397" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2448740397?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult-sff">adult-sff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2448740397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15032439451842991389"><em>The Library at Mount Char</em> is a novel where you must not wish to arrive, but which you may approach stealthily, sideways. Yet even then, it comes rushing towards you like an oncoming train, unstoppable.<br/><br/>The novel begins, and it’s like a nightmare; you expect, each moment, to wake to relief.<br/><br/>Father is missing, and it’s an answer to a question unasked, just out of your reach. You sit very still, waiting for the next answer to come. Father is missing, but his Library is still standing, like a kind of </span>
  <span id="freeText15032439451842991389" style="display:none"><em>The Library at Mount Char</em> is a novel where you must not wish to arrive, but which you may approach stealthily, sideways. Yet even then, it comes rushing towards you like an oncoming train, unstoppable.<br /><br />The novel begins, and it’s like a nightmare; you expect, each moment, to wake to relief.<br /><br />Father is missing, and it’s an answer to a question unasked, just out of your reach. You sit very still, waiting for the next answer to come. Father is missing, but his Library is still standing, like a kind of awful memorial to him. It’s a place built to make you want to keep driving away from it—<em>literally</em>. For years, Father held the lives of the 12 children he kidnapped in his steady grip. For years, they all thought Father might be God.<br /><br />Carolyn, the protagonist of Hawkins’ nightmarish novel, was formed, alongside her siblings, in the desperate, keep-alive pattern of the years they spent at the Library, losing their innocence like the bloom off a dandelion while committing themselves to Father’s blood-drenched set lessons. They were smashed and spitted, torn to pieces, killed and killed, so that nothing so noble as love, or forgiveness, could ever claim space in them. But they have lived and grown to strength and Father is missing, and Carolyn is come looking for her vengeance.<br /><br />Father had set the fire, but Carolyn will provide the tinder to burn it all down.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“That’s the risk in working to be a dangerous person,” she said. “There’s always the chance you’ll run into someone who’s better at it than you.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />I’ve come to realize that the only stories that really matter to me are the ones I don’t, and can’t, understand. What’s mysterious, ambiguous, unfathomable. So naturally, <strong>I loved the <em>fuck</em> out of this book.</strong><br /><br />Spending time in this novel is an exercise in trust—trusting that though the author will take you to deep, dark places, he won’t abandon you there. <em>The Library at Mount Char</em> is full of eclectic, macabre details. The author lets the reader into his world abruptly, and the beginning of the novel brings with it the buzzing sense of a warning, the sounds that come a moment before wasps swarm. I felt like I was reading a mystery book with every third line missing, unable to shake off the suspicion that there was something hovering just on the edge of the pages, waiting to pounce if I looked directly at it.<br /><br />Through a fragmented narrative, we piece together Carolyn’s past, and much of the novel’s white-knuckled tension stems from the increasingly horrific flashbacks that the author wields with wicked skill. There is a tangible sense that Hawkins is holding out on the reader for effect, and that feeling of unreliability is particularly heightened by Carolyn whose thoughts run deep and silent, like subterranean rivers.<br /><br />Carolyn’s <em>rage</em> was a closed house, and it made me afraid. She is a very interesting character. There was gravity in her, something somber and bleak. Everything Carolyn did, she did it with the grim purpose of a ship, battened against a storm. The novel allows the reader only a peek of her motivations and plans, but the hint of it is as dangerous as a coiled adder. And it’s what constantly pulled me toward the pages as if by a hook in my chest.<br /><br />Carolyn’s relationship to Father—and her siblings—is another point of intrigue. Carolyn hates Father, but hate, it seems, binds as strongly as love. Father’s chief skill was excavating the souls of his charges, digging into their center, and like some sort of malefic cat with a ball of strings, tangling their emotions until they lost all distinction between love and hate. “<em>You can adjust to almost anything</em>,” remarks Carolyn, chillingly, throughout the novel. And it’s that sentence that often echoed through my mind every time the narrative yields a new facet of the characters, and I struggled to reconcile what I thought I knew of them with what I’m reading before me.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“Step down into the darkness with me, child.” Just that once, Father looked at her with real love. “I will make of you a God.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />There’s a swirl of chaos at the heart of the story, yes, but the novel is tightly plotted and beautifully contained. <em>The Library at Mount Char</em> leaps from terror to terror. Things get nasty. Get bloody. Get complicated. But it’s <em>fun</em>, too, and for every string of violence, there's a welcome stretch of hearty banter. It’s clear that Hawkins knows exactly when to dole out the humor amidst the havoc, and his infallible ability to veer from terrible dread to downbeat comedy in the span of a paragraph makes for an incredibly thrilling ride.<br /><br />As for the ending, it felt like a déjà-vu—so familiar that it registered less as tragedy than as nodding predictability. But in a good way, and it was satisfying to see all threads connecting eventually.<br /><br />Hawkins’ heady brew of visceral horror is irresistible. <em>The Library at Mount Char</em> is a bracingly original, mind-blowingly twisty, and fiendishly clever novel. <strong>It’s also unlike anything I’ve ever read, and it’s all the better for it.</strong><br /><br /><blockquote>☆ <a href="https://ko-fi.com/kzabrekker" rel="nofollow noopener">ko-fi</a> ★ <a href="https://runawaywithdreamthieves.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> ☆ <a href="https://twitter.com/givemeabrekk" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> ★ <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">tumblr</a> ☆</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="15032439451842991389" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1139140590" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1139140590" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1139140590?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553418606" href="/book/show/23363928-the-library-at-mount-char">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1139140590" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4790834669392764798">i don't read a lot of fantasy. <br/>i read slipstream, magical realism, and horror, but fantasy typically just confuses me.<br/><br/>i think my obstacle is that with MR and slipstream, things are only just <i>slightly</i> tweaked, and what i relish is that unsettling feeling - that the possibility for fantastical occurrences is present, but there's still something concrete and recognizable to ground me. <br/><br/>my imagination is typically not strong enough for pure fantasy.<br/><br/>but that cover?? and a library??<br/>i was intrigued and </span>
  <span id="freeText4790834669392764798" style="display:none">i don't read a lot of fantasy. <br>i read slipstream, magical realism, and horror, but fantasy typically just confuses me.<br><br>i think my obstacle is that with MR and slipstream, things are only just <i>slightly</i> tweaked, and what i relish is that unsettling feeling - that the possibility for fantastical occurrences is present, but there's still something concrete and recognizable to ground me. <br><br>my imagination is typically not strong enough for pure fantasy.<br><br>but that cover?? and a library??<br>i was intrigued and ready to give it a shot.<br><br>and at first, i was not digging it. at all. for at <i>least</i> the first fifty pages i was all: holy shit what is happening is this part two of something what is going on?"<br><br>this book does not gentle you into its world. there are definitely elements that are "our-world;" character names like "michael," "carolyn," "david," there is mention of a post office, and horses and club soda, but there are also things like <i>Pelapi</i> and people coming back from the dead, a man wearing a helmet of blood and a tutu and another communicating with animals. <br><br>initially it is unclear when this takes place, if this is our world or just a <i>version</i> of our world, if there has been some sort of global event that forced people to live …differently and have different associations and only vague memories of <i>something called Reese's Peanut Butter Cups.</i> <br><br>but all will be revealed if you are a patient reader.<br><br>and it's pretty great. <br><br>in fact, i already want to read it again to see how those earlier scenes read now that i know all that i know. <br><br>because the book takes some unexpected turns. so many, in fact, that i'm not really sure how to review it without treading into spoiler territory. <br><br>at its most basic level it's a dark fantasy version of a bildungsroman in which orphaned children are schooled in esoteric and powerful arts by a man known as "father," whose lessons are dangerous and frequently cruel. they grow up in the flexible time of his library and are raised according to the ancient rituals of the pelapi, which distances them from the americans they once were. they never break into song like the charming orphans in <i>annie,</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419700110i/13114457._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>their particular lessons are harder, and turn them into harder people, prone to infighting, violence, and fear.<br><br>at the start of the book, father has gone missing, and without him in place the world, including our world, is in danger of his equally-powerful enemies making a power play. which would be very very bad.<br><br>unusual alliances are formed, there is a great deal of violence (for those of you with triggers - many animals are harmed. people, too - scores of them - but i know a lot of readers are more sensitive to animal deaths, so be warned), and the story is not at all concerned with who the reader may have become attached to - this is a harsh realm.<br><br>it's a vengeance plot with a long fuse that demonstrates that power doesn't just corrupt, it also dehumanizes.<br><br>i really enjoyed it, and i would be really interested to see what those of you with a deeper background in fantasy think of it.<br><br>but i do know that never has a tutu been more terrifying than it is here.<br><br>or has slapping a lion been funnier.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4790834669392764798" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1438950114" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1438950114" />
    <a title="Matthew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew"><img alt="Matthew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464987365p2/16254355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1438950114?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew">Matthew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781622317721" href="/book/show/25074701-the-library-at-mount-char">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=gr_awards_2015">gr_awards_2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=hoopla">hoopla</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1438950114" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15857396347421469129">What just happened?<br/><br/>This book is bizarre. This book is weird. This book is fantastic!<br/><br/>Sometimes books are complex, weird, and artsy - but it all feels forced. Kind of like the author sat down and said "check out how artsy and deep and meaningful I can be". I have some books in mind, but I will play nice *cough* American Gods *cough*. But, with this one it felt like all the bizarre complexity and weirdness was flowing out of the author and he couldn't help it. He sat down and said "OMG, what is com</span>
  <span id="freeText15857396347421469129" style="display:none">What just happened?<br /><br />This book is bizarre. This book is weird. This book is fantastic!<br /><br />Sometimes books are complex, weird, and artsy - but it all feels forced. Kind of like the author sat down and said "check out how artsy and deep and meaningful I can be". I have some books in mind, but I will play nice *cough* American Gods *cough*. But, with this one it felt like all the bizarre complexity and weirdness was flowing out of the author and he couldn't help it. He sat down and said "OMG, what is coming out of my mind right now!? It is awesome! I must be hallucinating! The world must share this acid trip with me!"<br /><br />What I am trying to say is that it was odd, I often had no clue what was going on, but I loved every second of it! <br /><br />I don't think this book is for everyone, and I think no matter how weird your tastes are, it will take a while to get into this. I am thinking I was 1/4 of the way through before I could put even the smallest coherent thought together. But, once you do, the great characters (pretty much all of whom were interesting in their own way), the creative dialogue, and the unique story come together for an experience not to be missed.<br /><br />I am looking forward to seeing what others think about this since it is so different than anything I have ever read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15857396347421469129" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553418606" href="/book/show/23363928-the-library-at-mount-char">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=cthulhu-goes-ph-nglui-mglw-nafh-ct">cthulhu-goes-ph-nglui-mglw-nafh-ct</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fanboy-goes-squee">fanboy-goes-squee</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=top-ten-w-cheats">top-ten-w-cheats</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2016-shelf">2016-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=reality-bending">reality-bending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=zombies-go-braaaaaaaaaains">zombies-go-braaaaaaaaaains</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=humor">humor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1391038681" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer785676929795357990">Re-read October 11, 2019<br/><br/>Just in case you might think that a book like this might lose its flavor or lessen my enjoyment three years after the last read, or it being the third read with the third-read blues, check your expectations at the door.<br/><br/>I still freaking love this book.<br/><br/>It has everything I could ever want. A mastermind plan or three. Godlike powers. A mystery, a revenge story, a freaking humorous and heartbreaking debacle including lions, dogs, and a very special man in a tu-tu, and a librar</span>
  <span id="freeText785676929795357990" style="display:none">Re-read October 11, 2019<br /><br />Just in case you might think that a book like this might lose its flavor or lessen my enjoyment three years after the last read, or it being the third read with the third-read blues, check your expectations at the door.<br /><br />I still freaking love this book.<br /><br />It has everything I could ever want. A mastermind plan or three. Godlike powers. A mystery, a revenge story, a freaking humorous and heartbreaking debacle including lions, dogs, and a very special man in a tu-tu, and a library that is so much more than a library.<br /><br />Where both rage and love can be the energy source of suns, and bitch-slapping lionesses is perfectly acceptable behavior. Or where standing up for yourself can usually mean several dozen suicides. Sequentially. For one man.<br /><br />Damn, I love this book. It has not lost any of its flavor. I could keep reading this every single year and still love it. It's definitely one of my all-time favorites. :)<br /><br /><br />Re-read October 14, 2016<br /><br />I read this one back in September of last year and loved it enough to drop it into my Top 100 list. I've been thinking about it off and on ever since then. And I just had to re-read it for the Halloween season, too. It just fits oh so well! :)<br /><br />Did it hold up to my beefed-up expectations? Did it lose any of the fires of ultimate agony or any of its Asshole Buddhism? Hello, No. :) I still love it.<br /><br />I've never loved lions as much as I have in this book. I've never been more surprised to discover a love story, either, or an actual loving Father in Adam Black, the man who by all rights should go down in all literature as the most fucked up villain of all time. <br /><br />All the oddness of this book, its sheer creativity, blows me away. All its characters become real and archetypes and real all over again, wrenched from all those endlessly tired grounds to become something new and fantastic again.<br /><br />You want to see the training of gods? You want to participate in a war of gods? From their point of view? Well, welcome yourself to this book, my friend. It's not for the weak of heart. The stakes are really high. Maybe higher than any but the strangest and strongest SF or Fantasy out there, and the wrap-up is frankly an even more awesome story than all the action that came before it.<br /><br />Expect an evolving story of unsurpassed creativity and courage.<br /><br />And even though the deaths, more deaths, and even more deaths, of world-eating plagues and starvation, of the snuffing out of the sun and the raising of a new one, it's kinda odd... that this is strangely one of the most up-beat and hopeful of Fantasies or Science Fiction or Horror that I've ever read. :)<br /><br />I might just have to make this a tradition and read it every year just for the plain joy of it. :)<br /><br /><br />Old Review:<br /><br />This one is going to be a difficult review because I love it so much.<br /><br />I'm not going to have Steve warm my bones under his light, anymore. I'm not going to have the thunder out of the east to have my back. But in the end, it is in Carolyn I trust. I have faith in her, and I'll have to have faith in her for the rest of my life.<br /><br />Confused? Read the book. You'll know what I mean afterward. :) <br /><br />My word, I can't get over how much new mythology that Mr. Hawkins crammed into such a short book, or how much of it wormed its way into my brain. I haven't been this enthused about any book like this since American Gods, and I have to admit this is a BETTER EXPRESSION than even that.<br /><br />Gods walking the earth is one thing, but to actually watch them perform an infinite regression of events to create their own successors in such a way that the poor sap doesn't even realize it until long after the big battle is a scale of craft that ought to be left to actual gods, and not some person named Scott Hawkins, who, out of the blue, blew my mind by actually pulling it off.<br /><br />I cried after Carolyn succeeded in getting her revenge, and I cried again after I realized what she had become by doing so. I don't need a heart coal to see me through to the end, though. I just cried like a little baby when Steve finally succeeded.<br /><br />This is an IMPORTANT work. It's going to stick in my mind for a damn long time, and even now the story is continuing in my hindbrain, either resurrected endlessly, or a victim of the Black Book. Or, maybe worse than any of that, it's going to stay with me because I Never want to let the story go.<br /><br />I'm recommending this for the Hugos for next year. It's not quite fantasy. It's more SF, and even Carolyn laughs at the notion of magic, so there you go. This novel is officially replacing my current top pick of Aurora by Kim Stanley Robinson, too.<br /><br />I am absolutely amazed by what I have just read, and I'm bumping this one up to one of my top ten novels of all time. It's just that good.<br /> <br /><br />Oh yeah, and if I ever get a chance to bitch-slap a lioness, you know I'm going to be blaming this novel. Just saying.</span>
  <a data-text-id="785676929795357990" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer6385772278678199606">This is a very strange book!<br/><br/>Reading the blurb I thought I was in for some sort of urban fantasy of the angels + demons, werewolves + vampires sort that often has a young woman in leathers on the cover showing an inch of midriff.<br/><br/>Nothing could be further from the truth.<br/><br/>This is a very brutal, rather crazy/flaky book that is so compellingly written it just drags you off on its bizarre journey.<br/><br/>The story opens on the small scale and stays there for a while, all the time stacking up the questions and l</span>
  <span id="freeText6385772278678199606" style="display:none">This is a very strange book!<br /><br />Reading the blurb I thought I was in for some sort of urban fantasy of the angels + demons, werewolves + vampires sort that often has a young woman in leathers on the cover showing an inch of midriff.<br /><br />Nothing could be further from the truth.<br /><br />This is a very brutal, rather crazy/flaky book that is so compellingly written it just drags you off on its bizarre journey.<br /><br />The story opens on the small scale and stays there for a while, all the time stacking up the questions and level of weirdness. It concerns the "children" of a godlike father-figure, each of whom have access to a very specific fraction of his vast knowledge &amp; power. Our main character (one of three points of view) has mastery of ... languages. Which doesn't sound like much, but she works it.<br /><br />Towards the end of the book the sense of scale accelerates rapidly, zipping through the US president and moving on to issues of planetary significance and beyond to jeopardise the solar system!<br /><br />The book has been highly successful. Its average rating is good but not sky high, and I suspect that this is to do with the way that the closing sections really don't make a lot of sense unless you are prepared to take a lot of random arm waving on board.<br /><br />I found I could swallow the end game weakness and thus ended up thinking the book was excellent.<br /><br />Surprisingly for a book set in the US, lions play a significant role in the story! Given my knowledge of lions (gathered solely by watching David Attenborough etc) I would say that Hawkins doesn't know much about lions (I don't think the male head of the pride goes hunting with his female cub ... I think the males laze around and the females hunt). But this is a minor niggle and I may be wrong! I actually really liked the lion sections.<br /><br />So yes, a very imaginative, very well written, intriguing, exciting, brutal, funny book that you should definitely give a go.<br /><br /><br /> <a href="http://eepurl.com/cimnK1" rel="nofollow noopener">Join my 3-emails-a-year newsletter #prizes</a><br /><br /><br />…...</span>

<div id="review_2408197241" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2408197241" />
    <a title="Sean Gibson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20955173-sean-gibson"><img alt="Sean Gibson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416866667p2/20955173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2408197241?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Gibson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Gibson" href="/user/show/20955173-sean-gibson">Sean Gibson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Sean by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/13286533-paula-w">Paula W</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2408197241" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11193258145619995670">Many people are familiar with Schrödinger's cat, a thought experiment developed by Austrian physicist Erwin Schrödinger in the mid-1930s. Essentially, the idea was this: if you put a cat in a box, to an external observer, the cat is equally likely to be alive or dead at any given moment (or, more accurately, simultaneously alive and dead—e.g., quantum superposition). Smarter people than I (of which there are many) can elucidate how the experiment suggests flaws in the Copenhagen interpretation o</span>
  <span id="freeText11193258145619995670" style="display:none">Many people are familiar with Schrödinger's cat, a thought experiment developed by Austrian physicist Erwin Schrödinger in the mid-1930s. Essentially, the idea was this: if you put a cat in a box, to an external observer, the cat is equally likely to be alive or dead at any given moment (or, more accurately, simultaneously alive and dead—e.g., quantum superposition). Smarter people than I (of which there are many) can elucidate how the experiment suggests flaws in the Copenhagen interpretation of quantum mechanics applied to everyday objects, but I’m going to apply it to another scenario.<br /><br />Let’s say you’ve experienced something weird that is difficult to articulate, but you really enjoyed it. So, you want to recommend it to people because you think they’ll dig it. But, the more you try to explain it and what you liked about it, the less likely they are to want to give it a shot, because it really is weird. And violent. And graphic. And mind-bendy. And kind of gross. And perplexing. And unusual. And sometimes a little bit funny. And sometimes a little bit dark. And sometimes a little confusing. And even a little non-sensical. And, so, when you describe it, people might be like, “Whoa, easy there, Tiger—I’m not into things that are simultaneously weird and violent and graphic and mind-bendy and gross and perplexing and unusual and a little bit funny and a little bit dark and a little confusing and a little non-sensical. I prefer cats, though whether they’re alive or dead, I don’t care.” <br /><br />So, you’re faced with a conundrum: you can try to explain this thing that you liked and get people to check it out, or you can just stick it in a box, not tell people what it is, and make them wonder whether it’s something they’d love, hate, or be indifferent toward, and hope that their curiosity induces them to check it out. Because, ultimately, it’s the kind of thing that only someone who’s intensely curious is going to enjoy. <br /><br />The latter method seems more effective to me, so I’m just going to stick The Library at Mount Char in this unmarked box here and leave it out on the Goodreads community counter. Hopefully, some of you will be insatiably curious and open it up at some point. <br /><br />(And it’s totally not my fault if it turns out that there’s a dead cat in there, too; I swear I fed the thing.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="11193258145619995670" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2408197241">
  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_1710249303" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1710249303" />
    <a title="Justin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2795921-justin"><img alt="Justin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528849864p2/2795921.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1710249303?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justin" href="/user/show/2795921-justin">Justin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1710249303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4989523402339061547">I'm staring at a blank screen trying to figure out how to even review this book. Outside the rain has been falling steadily for hours. I don't think it has any plans of slowing down today. The rain is a nice distraction. I can sit and listen to it while I sit inside and wrestle with coherency. I don't even know if that makes sense, but it sounds pretty impressive to me. <br/><br/>I really don't know where to begin. I mean, am I even reviewing the book anyway? Aren't my reviews just a bunch of jumbled thou</span>
  <span id="freeText4989523402339061547" style="display:none">I'm staring at a blank screen trying to figure out how to even review this book. Outside the rain has been falling steadily for hours. I don't think it has any plans of slowing down today. The rain is a nice distraction. I can sit and listen to it while I sit inside and wrestle with coherency. I don't even know if that makes sense, but it sounds pretty impressive to me. <br /><br />I really don't know where to begin. I mean, am I even reviewing the book anyway? Aren't my reviews just a bunch of jumbled thoughts with little to no prior thought so they're really my thoughts without me thinking about them but don't you have to think to have thoughts in the first place? <br /><br />The Library at Mount Char is the most fun I've had reading a book in a long time. I feel like I used that exact same line in another book review recently, but I lied if that's the case. This book really is the most fun I've had reading a book in a long time. If I use that line again in the near future, please remind me that I'm lying about that book, too. I think I've made my point way too clear at this point. I've gotta stop using the same word multiple times in the same sentence even if the meaning is different. <br /><br />I didn't really understand what I was getting myself into when I started reading. Hawkins just threw me into this world without any background information with the understanding that I would put the pieces together as I moved along. And I trusted him with that, and he didn't let me down in the end. I actually felt smarter as I turned each page up until the very end where everything is revealed. Now I feel like I need to read it again from my new vantage point. <br /><br />The world within these pages is awesome. One of the most creative stories I've ever read. You're not going to find anything to really compare it to since it's so unique. People have thrown around comparisons to Gaiman and I can see that. People have also compared this to Grossman's The Magicians, but that book sucks and no one should ever do that. The characters, the world in which they live, the writing... it's all so good. I felt the full spectrum of emotions while reading through this thing. It's hilarious at times, violent, thrilling, and even sad and depressing as it moves along. <br /><br />I really don't want to say anything about the story. It's almost better if you don't know much about it. Just give it several chapters. You're gonna have to learn it, and you will be handsomely rewarded in the end for sticking around. I promise. I've also been known to lie possibly so don't trust me. It's cool. <br /><br />Thanks, Kelley, for recommending this book to me. I didn't know it even existed until I got your recommendation. <br /><br />Now I'm recommending it to all of you. Clear your calendar and read this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4989523402339061547" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="mark monday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday"><img alt="mark monday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572672245p2/131922.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553418606" href="/book/show/23363928-the-library-at-mount-char">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to mark by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=super-private-journal">super-private-journal</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1644137319" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6353748966696862584">super fucking fun adventures with some super fucking powered librarians. it all gets very fucking dark; after all, it features the end of the fucking world. (kinda.) what's not to fucking like? <br/><br/>but why all the fucks, mark? this is an all-ages site! come on, man. restrain yourself. for teh children.<br/><br/>okay! this devious, bizarre, pitch-black, evilly sardonic, take-no-prisoners adventure novel is written by Scott Hawkins. it is his first piece of published fiction but it reads like he's been publishi</span>
  <span id="freeText6353748966696862584" style="display:none">super fucking fun adventures with some super fucking powered librarians. it all gets very fucking dark; after all, it features the end of the fucking world. (kinda.) what's not to fucking like? <br /><br />but why all the fucks, mark? this is an all-ages site! come on, man. restrain yourself. for teh children.<br /><br />okay! this devious, bizarre, pitch-black, evilly sardonic, take-no-prisoners adventure novel is written by Scott Hawkins. it is his first piece of published fiction but it reads like he's been publishing novels for years. I could not pull myself away from this book and I read my eyes out til the crack of dawn. crack cocaine for people like me who have no interest in crack cocaine but still want that exciting high. unlike many, my version of crack includes a novel whose first three-quarters are dense with action but whose last quarter is basically a series of melancholy and contemplative conversations between three characters about change, death, ptsd, empathy, and the natural and unnatural cycles of life. plus lots and lots of GOD. gimme!<br /><br />so here's a fucking story that I've probably already used in another fucking review:<br /><br />as a lad, I grew up in a household that was just not into the traditional concept of God, or into God at all. my dad was sort of an atheist and my mom was sort of an existentialist (which amounted to basically the same thing, to me at least). like most kids, I rebelled against my parents' rule. I did this by finding God. haha, that really came out of left field for my parents! this included accepting Christ as my personal savior, going to bible study, and a few summers spent at a religious camp. at the end of one such summer, the pastor had a practice of gathering us all together to answer any questions we might have. I had a classic one: <i>"If God truly loves us, why does He allow bad things to happen to us?"</i><br /><br />his reply was equally classic: <i>"Imagine a quilt. If you turn it over, all you can see are a mess of colors that make no sense and go nowhere. But the top side is God's side. And there you can see a beautiful pattern. That's God's plan. We don't see its beauty, but it is there, guiding us."</i><br /><br />I loved that answer! It made perfect sense to me. I came home excited to challenge my heretical dad and his outlandish lack of faith. I told him my big question and then I smugly recounted the pastor's golden answer. <br /><br />an approximation of my infernal father's reply: <i>"Well, genius, if God is so good, then why does he only show the shit side to us? Why doesn't he show us that other side and why does he hoard it all to himself? What kind of fucking God does that?"</i><br /><br />So I think it's safe to say that Hawkins shares my dad's perspective on God.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1275263586?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David - proud Gleeman in Branwen&#39;s adventuring party" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David - proud Gleeman in Branwen&#39;s adventuring party" href="/user/show/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party">David - proud Gleeman in Branwen&#39;s adventuring party</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=dashing-heroines">dashing-heroines</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1275263586" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12062589765453057869">This was my first buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/8409451-kristen' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Wonderful Kristen</a>, but it definitely won't be the last one ! It was a lot of fun discussing theories and comparing notes with you, Kristen! :D <br/><br/>I can honestly say this was one of the most bizarre books I've ever read! I read a lot of fantasy and science fiction, but this book was so unique and eccentric, it would blow the mind of even the most seasoned readers:<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533511958ra/26081994.gif' width='400' height='300' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Overall, I really enjoyed the book. Not only was it refreshingly original, but it was also laugh out</span>
  <span id="freeText12062589765453057869" style="display:none">This was my first buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/8409451-kristen" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wonderful Kristen</a>, but it definitely won't be the last one ! It was a lot of fun discussing theories and comparing notes with you, Kristen! :D <br><br>I can honestly say this was one of the most bizarre books I've ever read! I read a lot of fantasy and science fiction, but this book was so unique and eccentric, it would blow the mind of even the most seasoned readers:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533511958ra/26081994.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Overall, I really enjoyed the book. Not only was it refreshingly original, but it was also laugh out loud funny in some moments and cry out loud powerful in others. The casual prose while discussing outlandish events fit perfectly with the quirky nature of the novel. <br><br>I did have a couple of issues with the book. For one thing, it gets a little too grim for my liking at times. Some moments are very violent, to the point where it felt more like it was just for shock value than a necessary part of the story. Also, as strong as the novel is in the beginning, I felt it did collapse under its own weight in the final act. Fortunately, it all gets pulled together in the end to reach a very impactful conclusion.<br><br>A fun and emotional read, yet also one that requires a little patience and a really high tolerance of yucky stuff to get through. I'll write a much more coherent review once I've had time to gather my thoughts... right now I'm still trying to process everything that happened in this novel!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533513455ra/26082088.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4101865804184678873">MY BLOG: <a href='http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/02/the-library-at-mount-char-by-scott.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Melissa Martin's Reading List</a><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456685762i/18266605._SX540_.jpg' alt=' : ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Okay, I have to admit, in the beginning of the book to almost half way I wanted to stop reading and run away. I didn't like it or know what was going on half the time! <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456685762ra/18266606.gif' alt=' ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>My brain is not qualified for this book! <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456685762ra/18266607.gif' alt=' ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Then I started to really like it when the kids were in Mrs. McGillicutty's house with Steve, it got comical and I started understanding an eenie meenie bit more! :-) <br/><br/>I loved Steve's character. I thought he was a pretty good ole dude. I kinda like Caroly</span>
  <span id="freeText4101865804184678873" style="display:none">MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/02/the-library-at-mount-char-by-scott.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456685762i/18266605._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Okay, I have to admit, in the beginning of the book to almost half way I wanted to stop reading and run away. I didn't like it or know what was going on half the time! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456685762ra/18266606.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My brain is not qualified for this book! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456685762ra/18266607.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then I started to really like it when the kids were in Mrs. McGillicutty's house with Steve, it got comical and I started understanding an eenie meenie bit more! :-) <br><br>I loved Steve's character. I thought he was a pretty good ole dude. I kinda like Carolyn and I loved Michael and a few others. I couldn't stand David. Either way, this book is so bizarre and it goes back and forth from one thing to another just enough to almost collapse my brain! <br><br>Anyone can read from the blurb that these kids were adopted when their parents were killed by some bomb. They were adopted by the FATHER, he is a god, or God or something. He brought the kids to live in the library and they all had sections they were assigned to and they had to learn that all the time. Then FATHER goes missing, or is he missing? I can't even give a review it's so strange to try to do without some major spoilers. <br><br>These kids are very strange and they seem to die and come back to life a lot. The only part with David in it that I did like was when he did something to the President. Teehee, but I digress....<br><br>I loved the lions in the book as well. They were cool! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456685762i/18266608._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>All I can truly say is if your not liking the book at first give it a bit and then see. The whole half end of the book was awesome, the beginning for me, not so much. <br><br>I'm going to leave it with some of the funny EXCERPTS from the book:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453941928i/17893761._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>"Hello Steve," Carolyn said, her voice not quite a whisper. <br>"Hi!" he said, a little too brightly<br>"That's Mrs. McGillicutty. She speaks English."<br>"Yes. Yes, she certainly does."<br>Carolyn jerked her thumb at the couple behind her. "These are Peter and Alicia. They don't speak English. Not much anyway."<br>"What about the big guy out in the living room?"<br>"That's David. His English is pretty bad as well."<br>"And the other one? The one who keeps playing with the lighter?"<br>"That's Margaret."<br>"No English?"<br>"Hardly anything. She almost never talks."<br>"Can I ask you something?"<br>"Sure."<br>"Can you think of any reason I shouldn't grab one of those kitchen knives and stab you in the fucking neck?"<br>Carolyn pursed her lips, considering. "You might get blood on the cinnamon rolls."</i>
</b><br><br>••••••••••••<br><br><b>
  <i>Steve wanted to focus on the press conference, but he was having trouble. The big guy and the smelly woman were having some truly epic sex back there. It started with squeaking bedsprings, but those were eventually drowned out by bear noises and something not unlike yodeling. The smell of sex and rotting meat wafted throughout the house. Mrs. McGillicutty's bed evidently wasn't rated for stunt fucking, though. Right before the big finish it collapsed with a splintery, wrenching sound. Steve, not unimpressed, noted that the happy couple didn't so much as skip a beat.</i>
</b><br><br>**I would like to thank Blogging for Books for a print copy of this book in exchange for my honest review.**</span>

<div id="review_1309460925" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1309460925" />
    <a title="Dan Schwent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent"><img alt="Dan Schwent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593973948p2/870755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1309460925?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan Schwent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan Schwent" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent">Dan Schwent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553418606" href="/book/show/23363928-the-library-at-mount-char">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1309460925" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16893890382788228087">When Father goes missing, the Librarians he trained try to solve his murder while his legacy hangs in the balance. But what happened to him and who is responsible? More importantly, what will happen to His Library?<br/><br/><b>I got this from Netgalley.</b><br/><br/>I'm not completely sure how I felt about this book. Hell, for most of the book, I wasn't sure who was supposed to be the main character. However, I did enjoy it. Here's how it all went down.<br/><br/>Father, aka Adam Black, aka various other aliases, scooped up twelve o</span>
  <span id="freeText16893890382788228087" style="display:none">When Father goes missing, the Librarians he trained try to solve his murder while his legacy hangs in the balance. But what happened to him and who is responsible? More importantly, what will happen to His Library?<br /><br /><b>I got this from Netgalley.</b><br /><br />I'm not completely sure how I felt about this book. Hell, for most of the book, I wasn't sure who was supposed to be the main character. However, I did enjoy it. Here's how it all went down.<br /><br />Father, aka Adam Black, aka various other aliases, scooped up twelve orphans and spent three decades training them to be Librarians, the wielders of the knowledge he accumulated in his sixty-thousand year dominion over Earth. When he goes missing and the Librarians are barred from the Library, things go to hell quite quickly.<br /><br />Each of the twelve orphans has a catalog. Carolyn, whose catalog is languages, is the main character, although supporting characters Erwin and Steve get a lot of screen time. As the story unfolds, the backstory of the Librarians is revealed.<br /><br />The writing was pretty good and there was a surprising amount of humor. I thought the scheme the mastermind pulled off was very well done.<br /><br />As I write this review, it occurs to me that this is one of those books that I like the ideas way more than the execution. The magic system reminds me of The Magicians a bit and I love the idea of a nigh-immortal wizard training twelve orphans. However, I didn't really care about any of the characters other than Steve and the lions. I thought the story meandered all over the place and could have been more focused. It's also one of the few books where I wanted a lot more worldbuilding.<br /><br />All things considered, the Library at Mount Char was a pretty engaging read. I guess my only problem was that it wasn't the book I was expecting. Three out of five stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16893890382788228087" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1463283550" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1463283550" />
    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8836060-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487160141p2/8836060.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1463283550?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/8836060-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553418606" href="/book/show/23363928-the-library-at-mount-char">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1463283550" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5358944352872571436">I was at the library last week to pick up a book I was meaning to read. I never got that book. In its place (reserved for me) was this book. The librarian explained something about bar code errors to me but I really didn't care. I have already decided to give this book a try. The title was intriguing enough. I guess it was meant to be. <br/><br/>Not knowing what this book has in store for me (which is the most adventurous I will ever get!), I started on the first page, well… it’s about a librarian walking</span>
  <span id="freeText5358944352872571436" style="display:none">I was at the library last week to pick up a book I was meaning to read. I never got that book. In its place (reserved for me) was this book. The librarian explained something about bar code errors to me but I really didn't care. I have already decided to give this book a try. The title was intriguing enough. I guess it was meant to be. <br /><br />Not knowing what this book has in store for me (which is the most adventurous I will ever get!), I started on the first page, well… it’s about a librarian walking along the road with a detective’s blood all over her. Why in the world would I not read that immediately?<br />It was such a clever way to start a mystery book. It’s not a woman dead on the road. It’s not about the detective standing over her body. It’s about a woman who has just killed a detective, which sets you up for just how wild things are going to get.<br /><br />Of course, this isn’t actually a mystery book, either. The book is classified under “contemporary fantasy”, and I guess that will have to do. I don’t want to go into the plot too much because half the fun of this book is the slow, steady reveal of how weird and crazy things are. Suffice to say, I have not read anything like it before, and just when I thought I figured out what’s going on, I was sooner proven wrong. <br /><br />There are unending cruelties here. Psychotic families. Insane political machinations. Weird magic. Surprising twists. As awful as it may sound, I enjoyed reading this book! Not because I am beyond help, but the story is very enticing. It will grip you and hold you hostage until you get to the end. <br /><br />Any complaints I might have about this book were minor. There are some long talking scenes that repeat information to characters that I, as a reader, already knew. That was fine, it happens to the best of us. The pacing of the last act runs a little long, but again, by that point I didn’t care because the book was just laying down the payoff of the mysteries it promised to solve at the beginning, and I was fine with that. There are horrible things done to people. Horrible things! But it’s not voyeuristic and purposeless. There is a method to the horror and madness, and it’s treated fairly.<br /><br />I did not feel punched in the face, though there are certainly a lot of unanswered questions that I can’t really touch on without spoilers. Maybe another time... or just read the book, it will take you on a journey you will never forget!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5358944352872571436" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1317438197" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1317438197" />
    <a title="Edward Lorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn"><img alt="Edward Lorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492199506p2/8850418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1317438197?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Lorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Lorn" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn">Edward Lorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553418606" href="/book/show/23363928-the-library-at-mount-char">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who like anal nitrate, spam, and making adult decisions. </span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Edward by: </span>
      my book fairy
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1317438197" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18335407057805581350"><i>The Library at Mount Char</i> is one of the more original books I've read. It's been compared to the works of Joe Hill and Neil Gaiman. Content wise, I would agree. With that being said, it's nowhere near as well written as Hill's books, and vastly better written than Gaiman. Love Gaiman, don't get me wrong, but he'll be the first to tell you that he takes minimalism to a whole new level. And Hill? Well, Hill is just the man. If you don't fan-swoon over either of the aforementioned scribes, you'll l</span>
  <span id="freeText18335407057805581350" style="display:none"><i>The Library at Mount Char</i> is one of the more original books I've read. It's been compared to the works of Joe Hill and Neil Gaiman. Content wise, I would agree. With that being said, it's nowhere near as well written as Hill's books, and vastly better written than Gaiman. Love Gaiman, don't get me wrong, but he'll be the first to tell you that he takes minimalism to a whole new level. And Hill? Well, Hill is just the man. If you don't fan-swoon over either of the aforementioned scribes, you'll likely hate this book like a trip to the dentist. If you don't like weird shit in general, you're apt to drain your UTI onto its pages and keep right on steppin' without a fuck shown or given.<br /><br />Scott Hawkins has some fantastic ideas showcased herein. Dude has an imagination on par with Gerald Brom (<i>The Child Thief, Krampus</i>). Maybe a little Lovecraft thrown in because reasons. I don't read Lovecraft but I am familiar with his mythos and there was quite a bit of that on display here. There's even a mention of The Deep Ones (Lovecraft was... what? The Old Ones?). So, if you like Lovecraft you will probably like this far-out book. (Please don't try and convince me that Lovecraft is fantabulous and I should consume his literature ASAP. I don't like the guy or his writing, and that's all I need say on the subject.)<br /><br />One major complaint I had was the lack of character development. There is some tacked onto the ass end of the novel, but it felt like an afterthought. It's as if Hawkins said, "Oh, well, we've come this far with these characters, I guess it's about time to learn something meaningful about them." What we learn is good. The problem lies in the timing. At the point the character dev drops, it really doesn't matter if you love or loathe the characters. The meat of the book is gone and all that's left is the juice. This last-minute character dev seemed to be the optional slice of bread with which to sop up said juice. It's filling. It'll hit the spot. But it's not the same thing as <i>more</i> steak. <br /><br />Which brings me to the meat. Hot-fucking-damn is this book gory. If they ever manage to put to film the contents of this story we're talking a very hard R-rating. Guts on the ceiling, testicles removed, and a metric-fuck-tonne of blood are only a few things you'll come across. The horror fiend in me was giddier than a redneck at a Larry the Cable Guy show. You will also run into nuclear explosions and time travel. I'm telling you, sports fans, this book is fucking out there.<br /><br />In summation: I know I haven't told you shit about the plot, and I'm not going to. If you want a rundown, read the goddamn synopsis. I'm here to tell you what I liked or didn't like about the book. Will you like and dislike the same things? Fuck if I know. Should you spend your hard-earned coin to buy this book? I don't know. Can you afford it? Is your rent paid? Are your kids fed? Have you completed all your adult responsibilities for the month? Can you read it and return it within the seven-day grace period? Book buying like every other life choice is your decision to make as a discerning adult. I can hold your hand through the process but I can't make you like the book. All I know, padawan, is that the force was strong with this one, and I have no idea why I just went all Star Wars on your ass. Until next time, this is Harry Potter coming at you from Narnia with some timey-wimey supernatural bullshit. Holla!<br /><br /><b>Final Judgment: If I were an adult with an income, I would buy this book.</b><br /><br /><i>(Special note for my book fairy: Thanks for the swag, yo. You rock.)<br /><br />(Ridiculous note to Dan 2.0: This book is fucking ridiculous. Do not read this ridiculous book. Ridiculous shit happens with ridiculous consequences at an alarmingly ridiculous rate in this ridiculously fictional book. Did I mention it's a bit ridiculous? Because it is. Ridiculous that is. *ridiculously waves at Dan 2.0 and smiles ridiculously*)</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="18335407057805581350" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
