<div id="review_1274167321" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1274167321" />
    <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader"><img alt="Heidi The Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593309467p2/7986781.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1274167321?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi The Reader" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader">Heidi The Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553418606" href="/book/show/23363928-the-library-at-mount-char">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=the-numinous-book-club">the-numinous-book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=first-reads-giveaway">first-reads-giveaway</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=fantasy-and-sci-fi">fantasy-and-sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1274167321" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9730306370093648313"><i>The Library at Mount Char</i> is an urban fantasy/horror novel about Carolyn and her adopted "family" who are studying the seemingly endless knowledge of an immortal being that they call "Father." The lessons that they learn are terrifying but powerful.<br/><br/>After years of fear and torture at the hands of the Father and some of her siblings, Carolyn wants to break free from her living nightmare. She knows that she can't trust anyone, but she also doesn't know all of her Father's secrets.<br/><br/>How exactly does o</span>
  <span id="freeText9730306370093648313" style="display:none"><i>The Library at Mount Char</i> is an urban fantasy/horror novel about Carolyn and her adopted "family" who are studying the seemingly endless knowledge of an immortal being that they call "Father." The lessons that they learn are terrifying but powerful.<br /><br />After years of fear and torture at the hands of the Father and some of her siblings, Carolyn wants to break free from her living nightmare. She knows that she can't trust anyone, but she also doesn't know all of her Father's secrets.<br /><br />How exactly does one escape from a god?<br /><br />I think <i>The Library at Mount Char</i> is fantastic.<br /><br />The characters are more than human and divinely flawed, all of them.<br /><br />The plot proceeds at a breakneck pace, going from thrilling to apocalyptic so quickly that I couldn't put this book down.<br /><br />Yes, I lost some sleep reading <i>The Library at Mount Char</i>. If you pick this up, I bet that you will too.<br /><br />The distinctive mix of godlike powers and very human, emotional, knee jerk reactions contained in this story reminded me of some of the darker Greek and Roman mythological story elements like: the serial rapists (Zeus and about every other major god figure) and the unjust punishments of the innocents (Medusa, Actaeon, Laocoon, etc).<br /><br />Those mythologies were written to explain the unexplainable workings of nature, weather, time, and humanity itself.<br /><br />I think, if one makes <i>The Library at Mount Char</i> into a metaphor for reality, it fills the same role, in a modern way, as those more ancient stories.<br /><br />It gives a rhyme and reason to the mystery that is life. Pretty deep for a debut fantasy novel.<br /><br />Some of the twists I saw coming, but some of the big ones, I didn't.<br /><br />It kind of reminded me of an M. Night Shyamalan film, except instead of one gasp-worthy moment, there were maybe six of them.<br /><br />After each one, I'd put the book down for a second and start to rethink the story from the new vantage point that the author had just provided.<br /><br />It's really an amazing work for a first novel.<br /><br />Highly recommended for fantasy and horror fans. More sensitive or squeamish readers should keep walking.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9730306370093648313" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1527700004" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1527700004" />
    <a title="Cindy Newton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6082517-cindy-newton"><img alt="Cindy Newton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1432075684p2/6082517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1527700004?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cindy Newton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cindy Newton" href="/user/show/6082517-cindy-newton">Cindy Newton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553418606" href="/book/show/23363928-the-library-at-mount-char">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082517-cindy-newton?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082517-cindy-newton?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082517-cindy-newton?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1527700004" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8668380897327763526"><b>Review from 2nd Reading - 8/10/17</b><br/><br/>I still love this book SO MUCH!! The second reading only proved to me that my memory was correct, that this book is freaking amazing and as completely awesome as I remembered it being. The only thing missing, sadly, was the wonder of reading it for the first time. Otherwise, it's sublime! It's not for everyone--if you don't have a taste for the bizarre, if you're not willing to step outside the bounds of reality and embrace a fantastically skewed version of our w</span>
  <span id="freeText8668380897327763526" style="display:none"><b>Review from 2nd Reading - 8/10/17</b><br /><br />I still love this book SO MUCH!! The second reading only proved to me that my memory was correct, that this book is freaking amazing and as completely awesome as I remembered it being. The only thing missing, sadly, was the wonder of reading it for the first time. Otherwise, it's sublime! It's not for everyone--if you don't have a taste for the bizarre, if you're not willing to step outside the bounds of reality and embrace a fantastically skewed version of our world, then you're probably better off just not picking it up. While I respect your choices and your personal tastes, I still can't help feeling a little sorry for you. You will never experience the magic that is this book, and that's just sad to me!<br /><br /><b>Original review (2016)</b><br />This book is decidedly odd. After reading it, I wondered if it was just me. Maybe my reading choices have been so traditional and hide-bound that even the slightest deviation from the norm fascinates and perplexes me. I could imagine a great deal of collective eye-rolling and slightly pitying amusement by some GR readers, shaking their heads at my naivety in thinking this was strange. After reading other reviews, however, I discovered that I was not alone. This book IS odd. Some readers, however, felt distaste for its weirdness; I loved it! <br /><br />You start the story in total confusion and stay that way for most of the book. Information is released in tiny increments. Bizarre characters enter and fantastic events unfold; you scratch your head and keep reading. It does become clear, from the beginning, that there are realms of reality co-existing in this book. One is our normal one, going about its day-to-day business. That average world, with which we are so familiar, is completely oblivious of that second plane of existence, which is operating busily right under its radar. The inhabitants and events in this secret universe are largely unseen, and when they do collide with humanity, humanity suffers the worse of the encounter. <br /><br />The above is not a spoiler--you get this pretty quickly from our introduction to our main character, Carolyn, at the beginning. I won't say any more because I don't want to give anything away. I just think that this whole book, and the interactions between these two worlds, must have been an extremely delicate balancing act--one which Hawkins handled adroitly. It could so very easily have gone wrong; so easily have tipped over into absurdity, but it didn't. I believed in this universe he created; I bought into the existence of these characters and events, and felt the integrity of the resolution. He even managed to infuse quite a bit of humor into these strange happenings.<br /><br />I look forward to future books from this author, and hope he continues in this genre--he's well-suited for it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8668380897327763526" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6329586960866181082">4/5 stars<br/><br/><br/>Bonkers. Certifiably bonkers. (If anyone read that in Jason Mantzoukas’s voice, I’m in love with you.)<br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2017/02/14/the-library-at-mount-char-review/'>https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br/><br/>I’ve never read anything like this book before!! And I’m also pretty certain I never will again. It didn’t drip with gaudy description, but I could picture everything. I can’t remember the last time I felt that way. Also, I loved that like, the most insanely background characters were fuller than most YA protagonists. Because y’all know I’m a suck</span>
  <span id="freeText6329586960866181082" style="display:none">4/5 stars<br /><br /><br />Bonkers. Certifiably bonkers. (If anyone read that in Jason Mantzoukas’s voice, I’m in love with you.)<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2017/02/14/the-library-at-mount-char-review/">https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br /><br />I’ve never read anything like this book before!! And I’m also pretty certain I never will again. It didn’t drip with gaudy description, but I could picture everything. I can’t remember the last time I felt that way. Also, I loved that like, the most insanely background characters were fuller than most YA protagonists. Because y’all know I’m a sucker for a good character.<br /><br /><br />I like to think I’m a pretty smart person, but I was pretty much confused for the entirety of those 388 pages. Granted, I’m not really an expert on space or math or anything (English, you may not be surprised to learn, is my main schtick) but I did feel stupid every once in awhile (usually when I felt like my lack of understanding was making me miss a major plot point). Sometimes that was fine, and sometimes it was too much. <br /><br /><br />388 pages may not seem like a lot, but they were huge pages and a fairly small font and this book did drag a bit sometimes. (May have to do with how hard it could be to read.)<br /><br /><br />But I’m still givin’ it the big 4, because it’s so insane and imaginative and unique and really more of an Experience than a book. And you can’t undermine that.<br /><br /><br />Bottom line: if you have a lot of energy, a not-too-busy week, and confidence in your own intelligence that can withstand this, get your hands on a copy!!<br /><br />P.S. How'd I forget to mention how much I love this guy's writing style?! Like:<br /><br />Dear Mr. Scott Hawkins,<br />Do you have any grocery lists I can read? Also: thank you for your book. Also also: how in the hell did you come up with ANY of it.<br />Much love, respect, gratitude, etc.,<br />Some idiot</span>
  <a data-text-id="6329586960866181082" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10899031671159021892"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442243174ra/16203794.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>12 children are abducted by a powerful man and are tasked with learning his collected knowledge of the earth's secrets.<br/><blockquote>"I don't get it."<br/>"I'm not sure I do either, honestly. I mean, I know <i>what</i> he did to us, but I really don't have any idea <i>why</i>."<br/>p. 239</blockquote><br/>At times reminding me of bits of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1080717941?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>American Gods</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/577787836?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Magicians</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23363928.The_Library_at_Mount_Char' title='The Library at Mount Char by Scott Hawkins' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Library at Mount Char</a> is both interesting and pretty messed up.   <span id="freeText10899031671159021892" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442243174ra/16203794.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>12 children are abducted by a powerful man and are tasked with learning his collected knowledge of the earth's secrets.<br><blockquote>"I don't get it."<br>"I'm not sure I do either, honestly. I mean, I know <i>what</i> he did to us, but I really don't have any idea <i>why</i>."<br>p. 239</blockquote><br>At times reminding me of bits of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1080717941?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">American Gods</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/577787836?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">The Magicians</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23363928.The_Library_at_Mount_Char" title="The Library at Mount Char by Scott Hawkins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Library at Mount Char</a> is both interesting and pretty messed up. There are scenes with tons of dogs being brutally murdered and people being burned to death in a grill shaped like a bull. Not to mention that the kids grow up to pretty much be sociopaths, with the rape and murder and such. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407259145ra/10664326.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book also climaxes too fast, with the last third of the novel being falling action from the big confrontation. Don't get me wrong, we need that falling action because that's when the most interesting parts of the library are shown, but very little actually happens during that last 120 pages or so. I don't know how to rate this book. There are parts that were very entertaining, but there were others that were basically info dumps that had no importance to the story later on, and other things like the people with the reality virus who were growing tentacles for fingers were never expanded upon.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442244596i/16203920._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>

<div id="review_2709042708" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2709042708" />
    <a title="Jenna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3536004-jenna"><img alt="Jenna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535136437p2/3536004.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2709042708?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenna" href="/user/show/3536004-jenna">Jenna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553418606" href="/book/show/23363928-the-library-at-mount-char">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jenna by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/51370861-monumenttodecency">MonumentToDecency</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3536004-jenna?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2709042708" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer203777341866673376"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1558985538ra/27579805.gif' width='381' height='214' alt='Sorting Books GIF - SortingBooks Books Librarian GIFs' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>If the woman above is how you think of librarians, you probably haven't visited a library in recent years. And you certainly haven't read Scott Hawkins' amazing novel <i>The Library at Mount Char</i>. <br/><br/>Meet a few of the librarians:<br/><br/>•<b>Carolyn</b> <br/>Garbed in a reindeer sweater, 80s-style leg warmers, and Spandex bicycle shorts, our MC has mastered every language ever used on Earth, including those of all the animals.<br/><br/>•<b>David</b><br/>Though he dresses in a purple tutu, David is anything but a sissy. In fact, he is a ruthles</span>
  <span id="freeText203777341866673376" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1558985538ra/27579805.gif" width="381" height="214" alt="Sorting Books GIF - SortingBooks Books Librarian GIFs" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If the woman above is how you think of librarians, you probably haven't visited a library in recent years. And you certainly haven't read Scott Hawkins' amazing novel <i>The Library at Mount Char</i>. <br><br>Meet a few of the librarians:<br><br>•<b>Carolyn</b> <br>Garbed in a reindeer sweater, 80s-style leg warmers, and Spandex bicycle shorts, our MC has mastered every language ever used on Earth, including those of all the animals.<br><br>•<b>David</b><br>Though he dresses in a purple tutu, David is anything but a sissy. In fact, he is a ruthless killer, with a helmet made of blood and hair, and a string of intestines slung over his shoulder.<br><br>•<b>Margaret</b><br>"A creepy lady who smells like dead ass," Margaret studies the forgotten worlds, the places where we live before we are born and after we die. As such, she spends her life dying in order to travel to where the living cannot. Margaret enjoys licking tears from the cheeks of dead men.<br><br>•<b>Jennifer</b><br>The most normal of the bunch, Jennifer is the librarian who specialises in the healing arts. At first glance and compared to some of the others, she has a fairly decent career. However, we learn early on that her job is not one to envy. After all, someone has to bring Margaret back to life each time she dies. This entails performing CPR on a days-old rotting corpse, placing her mouth on a mouth full of wriggling maggots. <br><br>•<b>Father</b><br>One of the most sadistic characters, if not <i>the</i> most sadistic character, I've come across in fiction, Father is thousands of years old and has written the books contained in the world's largest library (the one at Mount Char), cataloging all of the knowledge of all times. When Carolyn's and 11 other children's parents are killed, Father adopts them all and begins training them to be Librarians. The ways in which he does so are..... are.... well, let's just say he would never win the Parent of the Year award. <br><br><br>If someone had described this book in detail to me, I would have sworn I would hate it. Instead, I absolutely, 100-percent <i>loved</i> this book! The horrors and gore were at times overwhelming, and yet.... and yet I could not stop reading this! Scott Hawkins, how the hell has he not published more novels??? This man is a genius! He is Stephen King on LSD. This book is incredibly imaginative, the characters so real even as they are fantastical. The world building, the character building, abso-freaking-lutely <i>everything</i> about this book is AMAZING!<br><br>I won't write more, don't want to give anything away. I think most people who enjoy fiction, even if you're not a huge fan of horror or fantasy, will enjoy this book. Oh, and if you <i>do</i> still think librarians are stern-faced, bun-wearing, shushing-you old ladies, you need to visit your local library. You just might discover that we are now tattooed and pierced and sporting purple and blue and green hair, laughing out loud and inviting you to do the same. Librarians are <i>cool</i>! However, if you happen to see some big dude who is dressed in a purple tutu, bloody intestines slung over his shoulder? -- <b>RUN!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="203777341866673376" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3550029720" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3550029720" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3550029720?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3550029720" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8380215022854056911"><b>DNF at 30%.</b><br/><br/>I tried, I really did. Practically every reviewer liked the book, my every single GR friend liked it (with one notable exception: Hi, Sarah!). Me: I used all of my willpower reserves to keep reading, but by the time I hit 30% mark I realized I was never into hardcore masochism. I quit. Forgive me <s>father</s> friends, for I <s>have sinned</s> am weak. <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1603156568i/30260302._SX540_.jpg' alt='Forgive' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Everybody and heir brother kept telling me the story is confusing. I say, "The story is as straightforward as the shortest path between two points i</span>
  <span id="freeText8380215022854056911" style="display:none"><b>DNF at 30%.</b><br><br>I tried, I really did. Practically every reviewer liked the book, my every single GR friend liked it (with one notable exception: Hi, Sarah!). Me: I used all of my willpower reserves to keep reading, but by the time I hit 30% mark I realized I was never into hardcore masochism. I quit. Forgive me <s>father</s> friends, for I <s>have sinned</s> am weak. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1603156568i/30260302._SX540_.jpg" alt="Forgive" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Everybody and heir brother kept telling me the story is confusing. I say, "The story is as straightforward as the shortest path between two points in Euclidean geometry." The disjoint way the story is told jumping from one episode to another back and forward in time makes it confusing. May I recommend Finnegans Wake by James Joyce as a really confusing story? <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1603156426i/30260286._SX540_.jpg" alt="Finnegans Wake" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This is just the best-known one, I can come up with numerous other examples. <br><br>So the the way the story is told makes it incoherent, especially in the beginning. I could not care less about any of the characters of the book. If at any point a giant meteorite had fallen down on Earth <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1603156656i/30260304.jpg" alt="Meteorite" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>killing all of them the only emotion I would have had would be a great relief they were finally put out of they misery. My misery too, would be over. No such luck unfortunately. <br><br>I could not care less about anybody to such extent that the famous BBQ scene <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1603156747i/30260306._SX540_.jpg" alt="BBQ" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>which supposed to deliver a great shock, made me yawn so hard I was at risk of dislocating my jaw. One of the character introduced (they were introduced all the way until I DNF) was a supposedly good guy working for Homeland Security. You know, that organization whose sole purpose is to come up with yet another imaginary bitter enemy within US soil? From Muslim Terrorists™ to Russian Hackers™ to White Supremacists™. They are good at creating these out of the thin air, I grant that. What I was saying had his guy been working in Kitten Rescue R Us <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1603156869i/30260309._SX540_.jpg" alt="Kitten Rescue" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>he would have a good shot at being somebody to root for. As things stand now: nope, don't care.<br><br>The plot: a being with a god-like powers collected twelve children and developed supernatural powers in them - different one in each. Suddenly he (it?) disappeared and the children not being used to a normal life had no clue what to do. To fight boredom and just to do something they decided to kill a bunch of innocent bystanders. This is the plot as far as I was able to see. And yes, I know there is a great design to all of this, but I could not care less about it. If fact I do not even feel like reading a synopsis of the book to see how it all turns out. <br><br>At this point I have to apologize for lying: I said I did not care about any of the characters. This is simply not true. I felt real pity for those bystanders. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1603156975i/30260329._SX540_.jpg" alt="Bystanders" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>None deserved an early demise. But the grown-up kids were bored, so...<br><br>I could not help making some comments on the last paragraph of the blurb. I am sorry, but it (the paragraph) asked for it. The text in bold is mine. <br><br><i>Populated by an unforgettable cast of characters <b>(ha-ha, I already forgot them)</b> and propelled by a plot that will shock you again and again <b>(put me to sleep again and again)</b>, The Library at Mount Char is at once horrifying and hilarious <b>(hilarious only if you find killing people is funny)</b>, mind-blowingly alien and heartbreakingly human <b>(I failed to find any traces of humanity in the main characters)</b>, sweepingly visionary and nail-bitingly thrilling <b>(so thrilling I cured my insomnia)</b>—and signals the arrival of a major new voice in fantasy <b>(no, I will not make any personal remarks about the author; it is not his fault I did not like his book)</b>.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="8380215022854056911" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1689354170" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1689354170" />
    <a title="Celeste" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste"><img alt="Celeste" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481055226p2/7317186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1689354170?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celeste" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celeste" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste">Celeste</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553418606" href="/book/show/23363928-the-library-at-mount-char">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=new-weird">new-weird</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1689354170" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12853915148185080490"><b>Full review now posted!<br/>You can find this review and more at <a href='http://booknest.eu' rel='nofollow noopener'>Booknest</a>.</b><br/><br/>Have you ever bought a book and not gotten around to reading it until years later? This is a constant problem for me, because I might have the teensiest book-buying addiction. I currently have well over 3,000 books in my home, many of which I bought because they were incredibly cheap, not to mention that I wanted to take them home with me because they had words in them. I have more books than I will probably ever be able to rea</span>
  <span id="freeText12853915148185080490" style="display:none"><b>Full review now posted!<br />You can find this review and more at <a href="http://booknest.eu" rel="nofollow noopener">Booknest</a>.</b><br /><br />Have you ever bought a book and not gotten around to reading it until years later? This is a constant problem for me, because I might have the teensiest book-buying addiction. I currently have well over 3,000 books in my home, many of which I bought because they were incredibly cheap, not to mention that I wanted to take them home with me because they had words in them. I have more books than I will probably ever be able to read. Does that stop me from buying more? Nope! My shelves have turned into something akin to archeological sites; I never know what I’ll dig up when I start looking for my next read. <br /><br />The Library at Mount Char was my most recent rediscovery. I bought it two years ago because it had a pretty cover (with the word “library” in the title, no less) and was on sale, but I somehow never got around to reading it. When I plucked it from behind the stuffed Totoro it was hiding behind, I got incredibly excited. The synopsis sounded weird and fabulous, and I wanted to start reading it immediately. Alas, now my reading is a bit more structured, so I had to pencil it into my schedule. <br /><br />The day arrived. I picked up the book and started reading. And I almost put it down. The first fifty pages of it were so dark, so bleak, that it was almost too much for me. There was child abuse and human sacrifice and poor victims resurrected to endure the torture over and over again until they grasped whatever lesson was being taught. Although the Library itself sounds amazing, it’s not a place I would ever in a million years want to visit. The hopelessness of the situation and the feral self-preservation that defined the students was just about enough to convince me to return the book to its hiding place behind Totoro. <br /><br />“You can adjust to almost anything.”<br /><br />But I’m glad I didn’t. I read the last two hundred pages in less than three hours. I can’t even tell you exactly what kept me so engaged, except that it was incredibly unpredictable. I’ve never read anything like it. Carolyn and Steve, the story’s main characters, continued to grow and surprise and sometimes horrify. Both characters had far more depth than I anticipated when they first appeared on the scene. Steve was the only genuinely good person in the book. He had a past, and he made mistakes, but he was good down to his toenails. But Carolyn, the true protagonist, was the real surprise for me. I understood her motivations, even when they made me super uncomfortable. Her intellectual rigor was so impressive. I loved this quote describing her:<br /><br />“Carolyn’s eyes were like granite, against which soft things might smash and be broken.”<br /><br />There was never a dull moment in this little book. There were epic lions battling packs of completely insane dogs. There were zombies in suburbia. There was the most terrifying barbecue pit on the face of the earth. There was a psychotic warmonger in a tutu and his girlfriend who liked to lick the tears from the decapitated heads of his victims. (They liked to finish off their sex-capades by killing each other and having their incredibly stoned physician resurrect them. Seriously, they were so disturbing.) We get to meet the Sun and a tiger god and the President of the United States. This was one of the most varied casts I’ve ever read.<br /><br />All in all, The Library at Mount Char was one of the most unique books I’ve ever read, if also one of the darkest and most irreverent. I recommend this book to those who can handle that darkness and the depression it often brings with it. Maybe balance it out with a Disney movie or two. Moana worked for me. If you do decide to pick this book up, I can promise you that you won’t be bored!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12853915148185080490" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7732444364249619770">I don't exactly know what to say after finishing this book other than I can't find the words to review it right now. I will say that I have never read a book quite like it (and I've read some weird books). I'm not sure how someone's brain houses a story like this and then can translate it onto a page but Mr. Hawkins has managed to do it. In short, the book is disturbing, freakout weird, compelling, original, and mostly brilliant. Full review when I can handle it.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2311956878024838443">Holy crap. I. Can't. Even.<br/><br/>This book - it's like everything I've ever wanted in my fiction, and so much more. It's like if bizarro and fantasy met literary for a twisted menage a trois. I was captivated from the first five minutes, and didn't want to pause the audio to even shower. <div id="review_1476093280" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1476093280" />
    <a title="Kelly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/94602-kelly"><img alt="Kelly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521304176p2/94602.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1476093280?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly" href="/user/show/94602-kelly">Kelly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553418606" href="/book/show/23363928-the-library-at-mount-char">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/94602-kelly?shelf=its-the-quiet-ones">its-the-quiet-ones</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/94602-kelly?shelf=fantasy-and-scifi">fantasy-and-scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/94602-kelly?shelf=great-and-terrible-men">great-and-terrible-men</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/94602-kelly?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/94602-kelly?shelf=grand-opera">grand-opera</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/94602-kelly?shelf=coming-soon-to-a-blog-near-you">coming-soon-to-a-blog-near-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/94602-kelly?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1476093280" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8688919224162206747">This review first appeared on my blog <a href='http://shouldacouldawouldabooks.com/2015/12/28/shoulda-coulda-woulda-books-library-at-mount-char-by-scott-hawkins/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shoulda Coulda Woulda Books</a>.<br/><br/><br/>I can't say I ever expected to write a review about how I almost cried over a lion-on-ghost-dog fight in the streets of suburbia, but here we are. Turns out it exists, the book that can make you do that. And it's this one.<br/><br/><i>The Library at Mount Char</i> tells the story of Carolyn Sopaski. What her story is we only gradually find out in fits and starts over the course of the novel, but at the beginning what we know is that Carolyn and he</span>
  <span id="freeText8688919224162206747" style="display:none">This review first appeared on my blog <a href="http://shouldacouldawouldabooks.com/2015/12/28/shoulda-coulda-woulda-books-library-at-mount-char-by-scott-hawkins/" rel="nofollow noopener">Shoulda Coulda Woulda Books</a>.<br /><br /><br />I can't say I ever expected to write a review about how I almost cried over a lion-on-ghost-dog fight in the streets of suburbia, but here we are. Turns out it exists, the book that can make you do that. And it's this one.<br /><br /><i>The Library at Mount Char</i> tells the story of Carolyn Sopaski. What her story is we only gradually find out in fits and starts over the course of the novel, but at the beginning what we know is that Carolyn and her "siblings" are "librarians" in a very unusual and intense library. Each of them is in charge of a section of knowledge- healing, war, mathematics, speaking to animals, or Carolyn's specialty, languages- knowledge gained in such depth that they have acquired a mastery acute enough to appear to be magic. They are ruled over by "Father", a sinister, powerful figure who adopted them all after an unspecified disaster and put them on their course of study and gave them the sort of abusive childhood that you might imagine the a child of Ramsay Snow and someone even more psychologically astute in the worst ways of torture might have created. (Perhaps I can best illustrate the brutality pictured by saying that one of the most horrifying features of this upbringing is that there was literally no way out. You could be resurrected if you tried suicide- and then punished even worse for having tried it. And you probably tried that suicide after one of your dear siblings killed you on purpose. For fun.)<br /><br />Carolyn and her siblings stir up a great deal of trouble for a great many people after Father suddenly goes missing, and, as they work towards finding him, they make their presence in the everyday reality of America known increasingly terrifying and hard-to-ignore ways. And then, of course, things really go to shit. <br /><br />....And it's absolutely fantastic.<br /><br />The plot is the major high point of this novel- I read a lot of books that nearly totally dispense with plot so I don't need a great plot to love a novel, but when it's well done like this, it is truly a pleasure to behold. <i>Especially</i> since he's able to really walk a tightrope of throwing us into the action of the plot right away and keeping up the pace without having us be too confused about what's going on. Mostly that's due to the excellent work he does with structure. He intersperses present-day plot with flashbacks that dispense background, information and character revealing anecdotes as needed, but without ever really detracting from the atmosphere, suspense or tension of the novel, which is quite something. He always explains <i>just enough</i> but not too much-enough to make you think you've got your bearings and want to know more before we move on. The beats of it are perfect- this is the rhythm of someone who understands what the reader needs to feel like to stay inside the story and stay invested in the characters, and how many resources he needs to allocate to each of those tasks.<br /><br />There are also, I must say, some wonderfully suspenseful action sequences throughout this novel, and this despite my own personal tendency to find standard action sequences rather boring these days. But Hawkins made them anything but boring by presenting them as scenes of ugly, brutal chaos with touches of the shockingly banal, without ever romanticizing what's happening: and also injecting a great deal of gallows humor into the thing. But he is relentlessly mundane in his descriptors, and smartly uses some true Everymen to inject some decency into the increasingly insane cast of characters in a way that sometimes adds to the hilarity, but can also tip the scales of what's going on into true poignancy (I'm telling you! That lion situation! I couldn't handle it!). The reader can easily imagine themselves in the settings but without ever feeling pandered to.<br /><br />And beats of the story as it winds up! Well done. This is one of the few books whose end I absolutely loved to the extent that I hope there is no sequel. The ending was so perfect and made so much sense and while I would like to know what happened next, I don't really want to know because it will be much better left unsaid, you know? It's the perfect kind of unsatisfied feeling. <br /><br />But while the plot work and story structure is what stands out above all, I would like to put in a word for some of the character work. Partially, I think the characters were as affecting as they were due to Hawkins' wonderful command of atmosphere- he did a great job with description, both inside and outside his characters' heads, and his tone and dialogue were huge points in his favor that made it easy to attach to his characters and get sucked into their world. I also think the slow reveal of Carolyn's true nature was really well done, especially the part where it turns out she doesn't know her true nature and what she's capable of herself. Not to mention a very entertaining and weirdly poignant secondary cast. Erwin is a cinematic type character and work of genius- I hope this book gets a movie made out of it just so someone has the opportunity to say some of his lines out loud. What a waste if they didn't! Steve is memorable and affecting and hilarious (and oh my god- his ending! I don't want to say any more, but those of you who have read this, let's talk below about how much we love it!), Margaret and David are burned into your brain whether you want them there or not, and Father.... Well. This is one of those times I want you to complete the list yourself because there are more names I could add, but I'd rather you find them for yourself.<br /><br />The reason I'm withholding the fifth star is basically only because of some nitpicks. The "magic" (not really magic, I know) was kind of hand-wavy and while some of the explanations/metaphors associated with it were funny, they never really made sense even in the abstract. Mostly it was amusing so I let it pass, but as its role became stronger it became harder and harder to ignore. Also, while I love some obscenity as much as the next person, I do think that Hawkins could probably rely less on having his characters use as many iterations as he can of the word"fuck" to get a laugh -it got less funny as he went on. I also think that fleshing out the other siblings who didn't get as much screen time would have been worth doing- the book could have been a little longer and spent a little more time setting up all these characters- it would have just made what happened later all the more heartbreaking. I think that was a missed opportunity.<br /><br />But you know what, none of that really matters, in the end. I had to think about it to really come up with anything that bothered me. If this had been a movie, I would have walked out of it excited and high-fiving people with overflowing energy. I basically did the equivalent of that in my own home, which amounted to a lot of babbling to my husband and leaping about, gesticulating wildly, and repeating "fucking amazing" a whole lot (I guess he infected me with his favorite word by the end, whether I liked it or not.)<br /><br />Unreservedly recommended to fantasy and sci-fi fans, urban fantasy fans, hell, even action/adventure fans. I'm stoked to see whatever crazy universe Hawkins comes up with next.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8688919224162206747" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1354761180" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1354761180" />
    <a title="♛Tash" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5451856-tash"><img alt="♛Tash" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456286012p2/5451856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1354761180?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♛Tash" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♛Tash" href="/user/show/5451856-tash">♛Tash</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553418606" href="/book/show/23363928-the-library-at-mount-char">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1354761180" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8896319837012694353">Review also on<br/><br/><a href='https://bookswithchemistry.wordpress.com/2015/10/21/review-the-library-at-mount-char/#more-3238/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433653616i/15127136._SX540_.png' width='350' height='117' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>The Library at Mount Char is the most bizarre book I have read. Ever. I don't throw superlatives around lightly, but this book earned it. I've been attempting to write my review for this for days now and between its grandiose premise and endless twists, I find it most difficult to review without giving out spoilers. I will try anyway.<br/><br/><b>God is missing</b>. God is known by many names, but he is Father to the Librarians. The Librarians were regular Americans once until Father adopted th</span>
  <span id="freeText8896319837012694353" style="display:none">Review also on<br><br><a href="https://bookswithchemistry.wordpress.com/2015/10/21/review-the-library-at-mount-char/#more-3238/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433653616i/15127136._SX540_.png" width="350" height="117" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The Library at Mount Char is the most bizarre book I have read. Ever. I don't throw superlatives around lightly, but this book earned it. I've been attempting to write my review for this for days now and between its grandiose premise and endless twists, I find it most difficult to review without giving out spoilers. I will try anyway.<br><br><b>God is missing</b>. God is known by many names, but he is Father to the Librarians. The Librarians were regular Americans once until Father adopted them to become Librarians. Each Librarian has a catalogue of expertise. There's the catalogue of murder and war, death, beasts, math and science, languages, healing arts and etc.<br><br>When Father disappeared, The Library that holds the secrets of the universe becomes impenetrable to the Librarians, so they must find a way to get in to find Father. Unable to find any other solutions, they decide to enlist the help of a normal American.<br><br>Carolyn, librarian of the catalogue for languages, goes out to the real world to seek the help of a plumber named Steve. Frizzy-haired, dressed in a chunky Christmas sweater over tiny bicycle shorts, Carolyn meets Steve in the bar and offers him the job. When Steve accepts it, he unknowingly set the motion that will change the universe as he knows it.<br><br>The book doesn't introduce itself or shake the readers hand on the first page, instead, it immediately asks to run alongside with it . It just goes on with its seemingly pointless and outrageous schemes for the first 10% or so.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Michael, like his cougars around him, was naked. David wore an Israeli flak jacket and a lavender tutu, crusty with blood. The flak jacket was his. The tutu was from the closet of Mrs.McGillicutty's son."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>This is the first time David and Michael were described and I had no context for whoever Mrs.McGillicutty was or her son at this point, so I was in a constant state of ...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1443107920ra/16319383.gif" width="304" height="169" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It is just fortunate that Scott Hawkins is a talented writer, so it makes the confusion bearable. A writer with lesser writing mojo couldn't have pulled this off, so kudos Mr. Hawkins.<br><br>At around 30% it started to make sense, though it maintained its ridiculousness (there's a tentacle lord named Barry O'Shea for chrissakes). Once it started making sense, it was fast-paced, violent and funny.It was unputdownable.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"That's the risk in working to be a dangerous person,", she said."There's always the chance you'll run into someone who is better than you."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>I have never read a book with a premise so well concealed, I only understood the real premise at around 80% mark and it was far grander than I initially thought. Like all stories with a similar premise, it involves deceit, murder and resurrection. If you can guess what the premise is from the quote above, then 300 points for Ravenclaw.<br><br>So why the 3.5 stars? Getting through the first 30% of the book was a tad difficult for me. It shouldn't be that hard and long to get into a book. There were also background stories I found unnecessary, while important details like the catalogues of other Librarians were severely lacking.<br><br>The Library at Mount Char is a well-written dark fantasy for adults. It's gritty, violent and thoroughly perplexing for the most part. This is the type of book that keeps the readers in complete darkness, until it is well and ready to reveal its secrets, so approach with caution and when you do read this, do not only suspend your disbelief, but bury it, and bury it deep.<br><br>----------------------------------------------------------<br>October 15, 2015<br><br>Idk, man, I can only describe it as confuzzling. 3.5 stars<br><br>Also, I want to adopt a lion from the shelter. Preferably, female and formerly owned by a gangsta rap star.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8896319837012694353" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2231699191" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2231699191" />
    <a title="Laura Noggle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47417894-laura-noggle"><img alt="Laura Noggle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521261175p2/47417894.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2231699191?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura Noggle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura Noggle" href="/user/show/47417894-laura-noggle">Laura Noggle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24579792-the-library-at-mount-char">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone looking for something to blow their mind.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47417894-laura-noggle?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47417894-laura-noggle?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2231699191" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13175833187090544560">5 Solid Stars: Surprising, Imaginative, Powerful 🤯<br/><br/><i>“Behind her eyes, black flowers bloomed.”</i><br/><br/>It’s hard to know where to start with this book other than … <b>WOW</b>. What a trip. Imagine if the movie <i>Mother!</i>, <i>Dr. Strange</i>, and an M. C. Escher painting had a baby — you might be close to capturing the essence of this psychotropic tome. <br/><br/><i>“The explosive brightness was startling in the long, dreamy shadows of this suburban afternoon.”</i> <br/><br/>Whichever way you look at it, this book is a wild ride you should definitely </span>
  <span id="freeText13175833187090544560" style="display:none">5 Solid Stars: Surprising, Imaginative, Powerful 🤯<br /><br /><i>“Behind her eyes, black flowers bloomed.”</i><br /><br />It’s hard to know where to start with this book other than … <b>WOW</b>. What a trip. Imagine if the movie <i>Mother!</i>, <i>Dr. Strange</i>, and an M. C. Escher painting had a baby — you might be close to capturing the essence of this psychotropic tome. <br /><br /><i>“The explosive brightness was startling in the long, dreamy shadows of this suburban afternoon.”</i> <br /><br />Whichever way you look at it, this book is a wild ride you should definitely take. Unlike any other book I’ve read, this book steadily climbed the “star ladder.” At first, I had no clue what was happening. The beginning is bizarre and took me a minute to buckle up. Things pick up speed, and soon you’re hurtling into unknown territory. Shocking and violent, the plot intensifies punctuated with dark comedy. I couldn’t put it down after halfway, and powered through to the end. It *almost* felt like two books, as the plot takes a sharp left turn and heads out past the cosmos. <br /><br /><i>“Warm air spilled out, dry as desert wind and heavy with the scent of ancient dust.”</i><br /><br />All I can say is read this book, and see for yourself. <br /><br />PS—I first heard of this book from this article: <i>
  <a href="https://www.npr.org/2017/12/23/573053135/just-trust-me-in-praise-of-strange-books" rel="nofollow noopener">Just Trust Me: In Praise Of Strange Books</a>
</i> — piquing my interest with: "Give me something dark … Give me a book that sunk its teeth into you. One that changed you, left you a little different by the time you were done.”<br /><br />The <i>Library At Mount Char</i> does not disappoint. <br /><br />(<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25733983.Lab_Girl" title="Lab Girl by Hope Jahren" rel="nofollow noopener">Lab Girl</a>, also recommended in the article, is another 5 star read.) <br /><br /><b>
  <u>Favorite Quotes:</u>
</b><br /><br />“Peace of mind is not the absence of conflict, but the ability to cope with it.”<br /><br />“No real thing can be so perfect as memory, and she will need a perfect thing if she is to survive. She will warm herself on the memory of you when there is nothing else, and be sustained.”<br /><br />***2019 Update: Still one of my all time favorite books.***</span>
  <a data-text-id="13175833187090544560" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zgfGzrmPJKlLD8dLV/S3rTkcgOcNO51Wuv6+V95HUC6duVqaTu5YernEn68mh8HO/CfUes1bkhureJzZraeDcQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zGk3gr/qeBuZ34nMSyXSBl0lSuIfliqO3XZw3482HI+f16vWSIsEyGsU0Sg6VqRlmB4ef9/2JcPM8FJR/NbP0A==')})
  }
//]]>

When Abe and Dan, two widowers who have found solace in each other\'s company and a shared passion for fishing, hear rumors of the Creek, and what might be found there, the remedy to both their losses, they dismiss it as just another fish story. Soon, though, the men find themselves drawn into a tale as deep and old as the Reservoir. It\'s a tale of dark pacts, of long-buried secrets, and of a mysterious figure known as Der Fisher: the Fisherman.
